## Orbit and rotation

Main article: [Orbit of Mars](/wiki/Orbit_of_Mars "Orbit of Mars")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Marsorbitsolarsystem.gif/220px-
Marsorbitsolarsystem.gif)](/wiki/File:Marsorbitsolarsystem.gif)

[](/wiki/File:Marsorbitsolarsystem.gif "Enlarge")

Mars is about 230 million km (143 million mi) from the Sun; its orbital period
is 687 (Earth) days, depicted in red. Earth's orbit is in blue.

Mars's average distance from the Sun is roughly 230 million km (143 million
mi), and its orbital period is 687 (Earth) days. The solar day (or
[sol](/wiki/Sol_\(day_on_Mars\) "Sol \(day on Mars\)")) on Mars is only
slightly longer than an Earth day: 24 hours, 39 minutes, and 35.244
seconds.[201] A Martian year is equal to 1.8809 Earth years, or 1 year, 320
days, and 18.2 hours.[10]

The axial tilt of Mars is 25.19° relative to its [orbital
plane](/wiki/Orbital_plane "Orbital plane"), which is similar to the axial
tilt of Earth.[10] As a result, Mars has seasons like Earth, though on Mars
they are nearly twice as long because its orbital period is that much longer.
In the present day epoch, the orientation of the [north pole](/wiki/North_pole
"North pole") of Mars is close to the star [Deneb](/wiki/Deneb "Deneb").[15]

Mars has a relatively pronounced [orbital
eccentricity](/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity "Orbital eccentricity") of about
0.09; of the seven other planets in the Solar System, only
[Mercury](/wiki/Mercury_\(planet\) "Mercury \(planet\)") has a larger orbital
eccentricity. It is known that in the past, Mars has had a much more circular
orbit. At one point, 1.35 million Earth years ago, Mars had an eccentricity of
roughly 0.002, much less than that of Earth today.[202] Mars's [cycle of
eccentricity](/wiki/Milankovitch_cycles "Milankovitch cycles") is 96,000 Earth
years compared to Earth's cycle of 100,000 years.[203] Mars has a much longer
cycle of eccentricity, with a period of 2.2 million Earth years, and this
overshadows the 96,000-year cycle in the eccentricity graphs.[ _[clarification
needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")_ ] For the
last 35,000 years, the orbit of Mars has been getting slightly more eccentric
because of the gravitational effects of the other planets. The closest
distance between Earth and Mars will continue to mildly decrease for the next
25,000 years.[204]

## Habitability and search for life

Main article: [Life on Mars](/wiki/Life_on_Mars "Life on Mars")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Mars_Viking_11d128.png/310px-
Mars_Viking_11d128.png)](/wiki/File:Mars_Viking_11d128.png)

[](/wiki/File:Mars_Viking_11d128.png "Enlarge")

_[Viking 1](/wiki/Viking_1 "Viking 1")_ lander's sampling arm scooped up soil
samples for tests ([Chryse Planitia](/wiki/Chryse_Planitia "Chryse Planitia"))

The current understanding of [planetary
habitability](/wiki/Planetary_habitability "Planetary habitability") - the
ability of a world to develop environmental conditions favorable to the
emergence of life - favors planets that have liquid water on their surface.
Most often this requires the orbit of a planet to lie within the [habitable
zone](/wiki/Planetary_Habitability_Index "Planetary Habitability Index"),
which for the Sun extends from just beyond Venus to about the [semi-major
axis](/wiki/Semi-major_axis "Semi-major axis") of Mars.[205] During
perihelion, Mars dips inside this region, but Mars's thin (low-pressure)
atmosphere prevents liquid water from existing over large regions for extended
periods. The past flow of liquid water demonstrates the planet's potential for
habitability. Recent evidence has suggested that any water on the Martian
surface may have been too salty and acidic to support regular terrestrial
life.[206]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/PIA19673-Mars-
AlgaCrater-ImpactGlassDetected-MRO-20150608.jpg/220px-PIA19673-Mars-
AlgaCrater-ImpactGlassDetected-MRO-20150608.jpg)](/wiki/File:PIA19673-Mars-
AlgaCrater-ImpactGlassDetected-MRO-20150608.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:PIA19673-Mars-AlgaCrater-ImpactGlassDetected-MRO-20150608.jpg
"Enlarge")

Detection of [impact glass](/wiki/Impactite "Impactite") deposits (green
spots) at [Alga crater](/wiki/List_of_craters_on_Mars:_A%E2%80%93G "List of
craters on Mars: A–G"), a possible site for preserved [ancient
life](/wiki/Life_on_Mars "Life on Mars")[207]

The lack of a magnetosphere and the extremely thin atmosphere of Mars are a
challenge: the planet has little [heat transfer](/wiki/Heat_transfer "Heat
transfer") across its surface, poor insulation against bombardment of the
[solar wind](/wiki/Solar_wind "Solar wind") and insufficient atmospheric
pressure to retain water in a liquid form (water instead
[sublimes](/wiki/Sublimation_\(phase_transition\) "Sublimation \(phase
transition\)") to a gaseous state). Mars is nearly, or perhaps totally,
geologically dead; the end of volcanic activity has apparently stopped the
recycling of chemicals and minerals between the surface and interior of the
planet.[208]

_In situ_ investigations have been performed on Mars by the [_Viking_
landers](/wiki/Viking_program#Viking_landers "Viking program"),
[_Spirit_](/wiki/Spirit_\(rover\) "Spirit \(rover\)") and _Opportunity_
rovers, [_Phoenix_](/wiki/Phoenix_\(spacecraft\) "Phoenix \(spacecraft\)")
lander, and _Curiosity_ rover. Evidence suggests that the planet was once
significantly more habitable than it is today, but whether living
[organisms](/wiki/Organism "Organism") ever existed there remains unknown. The
[Viking probes](/wiki/Viking_probes "Viking probes") of the mid-1970s carried
experiments designed to detect microorganisms in Martian soil at their
respective landing sites and had positive results, including a temporary
increase of CO  
2 production on exposure to water and nutrients. This sign of life was later
disputed by scientists, resulting in a continuing debate, with NASA scientist
[Gilbert Levin](/wiki/Gilbert_Levin "Gilbert Levin") asserting that Viking may
have found life. A re-analysis of the Viking data, in light of modern
knowledge of [extremophile](/wiki/Extremophile "Extremophile") forms of life,
has suggested that the Viking tests were not sophisticated enough to detect
these forms of life. The tests could even have killed a (hypothetical) life
form.[209] Tests conducted by the Phoenix Mars lander have shown that the soil
has an [alkaline](/wiki/Alkaline "Alkaline") [pH](/wiki/PH "PH") and it
contains magnesium, sodium, potassium and chloride.[210] The soil nutrients
may be able to support life, but life would still have to be shielded from the
intense ultraviolet light.[211] A recent analysis of martian meteorite
EETA79001 found 0.6 ppm ClO−  
4, 1.4 ppm ClO−  
3, and 16 ppm NO−  
3, most likely of Martian origin. The ClO−  
3 suggests the presence of other highly oxidizing oxychlorines, such as ClO−  
2 or ClO, produced both by UV oxidation of Cl and X-ray radiolysis of ClO−  
4. Thus, only highly refractory and/or well-protected (sub-surface) organics or life forms are likely to survive.[212]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Mars-Curiosity-
RockStructures-20180102.jpg/220px-Mars-Curiosity-
RockStructures-20180102.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mars-Curiosity-
RockStructures-20180102.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:Mars-Curiosity-RockStructures-20180102.jpg "Enlarge")

This image from Gale crater in 2018 prompted speculation that some shapes were
worm-like fossils, but they were geological formations probably formed under
water.[213]

A 2014 analysis of the Phoenix WCL showed that the Ca(ClO  
4)  
2 in the Phoenix soil has not interacted with liquid water of any form,
perhaps for as long as 600 million years. If it had, the highly soluble Ca(ClO  
4)  
2 in contact with liquid water would have formed only CaSO  
4. This suggests a severely arid environment, with minimal or no liquid water interaction.[214]

Scientists have proposed that carbonate globules found in
[meteorite](/wiki/Meteorite "Meteorite") [ALH84001](/wiki/Allan_Hills_84001
"Allan Hills 84001"), which is thought to have originated from Mars, could be
fossilized microbes extant on Mars when the meteorite was blasted from the
Martian surface by a meteor strike some 15 million years ago. This proposal
has been met with skepticism, and an exclusively inorganic origin for the
shapes has been proposed.[215]

Small quantities of [methane](/wiki/Methane "Methane") and
[formaldehyde](/wiki/Formaldehyde "Formaldehyde") detected by Mars orbiters
are both claimed to be possible evidence for life, as these [chemical
compounds](/wiki/Chemical_compound "Chemical compound") would quickly break
down in the Martian atmosphere.[216][217] Alternatively, these compounds may
instead be replenished by volcanic or other geological means, such as
[serpentinite](/wiki/Serpentinite "Serpentinite").[190]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Mars-SubglacialWater-
SouthPoleRegion-20180725.jpg/170px-Mars-SubglacialWater-
SouthPoleRegion-20180725.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mars-SubglacialWater-
SouthPoleRegion-20180725.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:Mars-SubglacialWater-SouthPoleRegion-20180725.jpg "Enlarge")

Location of subsurface water in [Planum Australe](/wiki/Planum_Australe
"Planum Australe")

[Impact glass](/wiki/Impactite "Impactite"), formed by the impact of meteors,
which on Earth can preserve signs of life, has been found on the surface of
the impact craters on Mars.[218][219] Likewise, the glass in impact craters on
Mars could have preserved signs of life if life existed at the
site.[220][221][222]

In May 2017, evidence of the [earliest known
life](/wiki/Earliest_known_life_forms "Earliest known life forms") [on
land](/wiki/Evolutionary_history_of_life#Colonization_of_land "Evolutionary
history of life") on Earth may have been found in 3.48-billion-year-old
[geyserite](/wiki/Geyserite "Geyserite") and other related mineral deposits
(often found around [hot springs](/wiki/Hot_spring "Hot spring") and
[geysers](/wiki/Geyser "Geyser")) uncovered in the [Pilbara
Craton](/wiki/Pilbara_Craton "Pilbara Craton") of [Western
Australia](/wiki/Western_Australia "Western Australia"). These findings may be
helpful in deciding where best to search for early signs of [life on the
planet Mars](/wiki/Life_on_Mars "Life on Mars").[223][224]

In early 2018, media reports speculated that certain rock features at a site
called Jura looked like a type of fossil, but project scientists say the
formations likely resulted from a geological process at the bottom of an
ancient drying lakebed, and are related to mineral veins in the area similar
to [gypsum](/wiki/Gypsum "Gypsum") crystals.[213]

On 7 June 2018, NASA announced that the _Curiosity_ rover had discovered
[organic compounds](/wiki/Organic_compound "Organic compound") in sedimentary
rocks dating to three billion years old,[225] indicating that some of the
building blocks for life were present.[226][227]

In July 2018, scientists reported the discovery of a subglacial lake on Mars,
the first known stable body of water on the planet. It sits 1.5 km (0.9 mi)
below the surface at the base of the [southern polar ice
cap](/wiki/Planum_Australe "Planum Australe") and is about 20 kilometres (12
mi) wide.[228][229] The lake was discovered using the [MARSIS](/wiki/MARSIS
"MARSIS") radar on board the _[Mars Express](/wiki/Mars_Express "Mars
Express")_ orbiter, and the profiles were collected between May 2012 and
December 2015.[230] The lake is centered at 193° East, 81° South, a flat area
that does not exhibit any peculiar topographic characteristics. It is mostly
surrounded by higher ground except on its eastern side, where there is a
depression.[228]

## Moons

Main articles: [Moons of Mars](/wiki/Moons_of_Mars "Moons of Mars"), [Phobos
(moon)](/wiki/Phobos_\(moon\) "Phobos \(moon\)"), and [Deimos
(moon)](/wiki/Deimos_\(moon\) "Deimos \(moon\)")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Phobos_colour_2008.jpg/172px-
Phobos_colour_2008.jpg)](/wiki/File:Phobos_colour_2008.jpg)

Enhanced-color HiRISE image of [Phobos](/wiki/Phobos_\(moon\) "Phobos
\(moon\)"), showing a series of mostly parallel grooves and [crater
chains](/wiki/Crater_chain "Crater chain"), with [Stickney
crater](/wiki/Stickney_\(crater\) "Stickney \(crater\)") at right

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Deimos-MRO.jpg/162px-
Deimos-MRO.jpg)](/wiki/File:Deimos-MRO.jpg)

Enhanced-color HiRISE image of [Deimos](/wiki/Deimos_\(moon\) "Deimos
\(moon\)") (not to scale), showing its smooth blanket of
[regolith](/wiki/Regolith "Regolith")

Mars has two relatively small (compared to Earth's) natural moons,
[Phobos](/wiki/Phobos_\(moon\) "Phobos \(moon\)") (about 22 kilometres (14 mi)
in diameter) and [Deimos](/wiki/Deimos_\(moon\) "Deimos \(moon\)") (about 12
kilometres (7.5 mi) in diameter), which orbit close to the planet. Asteroid
capture is a long-favored theory, but their origin remains uncertain.[231]
Both satellites were discovered in 1877 by [Asaph Hall](/wiki/Asaph_Hall
"Asaph Hall"); they are named after the characters
[Phobos](/wiki/Phobos_\(mythology\) "Phobos \(mythology\)") (panic/fear) and
[Deimos](/wiki/Deimos_\(mythology\) "Deimos \(mythology\)") (terror/dread),
who, in [Greek mythology](/wiki/Greek_mythology "Greek mythology"),
accompanied their father [Ares](/wiki/Ares "Ares"), god of war, into battle.
Mars was the Roman counterpart of Ares.[232][233] In modern
[Greek](/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language"), the planet retains its ancient
name _Ares_ (Aris: _Άρης_ ).[234]

From the surface of Mars, the motions of Phobos and Deimos appear different
from that of the [Moon](/wiki/Moon "Moon"). Phobos rises in the west, sets in
the east, and rises again in just 11 hours. Deimos, being only just outside
[synchronous orbit](/wiki/Synchronous_orbit "Synchronous orbit") - where the
orbital period would match the planet's period of rotation - rises as expected
in the east but slowly. Despite the 30-hour orbit of Deimos, 2.7 days elapse
between its rise and set for an equatorial observer, as it slowly falls behind
the rotation of Mars.[235]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Orbits_of_Phobos_and_Deimos.gif)](/wiki/File:Orbits_of_Phobos_and_Deimos.gif)

Orbits of Phobos and Deimos (to scale)

Because the orbit of Phobos is below synchronous altitude, the [tidal
forces](/wiki/Tidal_force "Tidal force") from the planet Mars are gradually
lowering its orbit. In about 50 million years, it could either crash into
Mars's surface or break up into a ring structure around the planet.[235]

The origin of the two moons is not well understood. Their low albedo and
[carbonaceous chondrite](/wiki/Carbonaceous_chondrite "Carbonaceous
chondrite") composition have been regarded as similar to asteroids, supporting
the capture theory. The unstable orbit of Phobos would seem to point towards a
relatively recent capture. But both have [circular
orbits](/wiki/Circular_orbit "Circular orbit"), near the equator, which is
unusual for captured objects and the required capture dynamics are complex.
Accretion early in the history of Mars is plausible, but would not account for
a composition resembling asteroids rather than Mars itself, if that is
confirmed.

A third possibility is the involvement of a third body or a type of impact
disruption.[236] More-recent lines of evidence for Phobos having a highly
porous interior,[237] and suggesting a composition containing mainly
[phyllosilicates](/wiki/Phyllosilicates "Phyllosilicates") and other minerals
known from Mars,[238] point toward an origin of Phobos from material ejected
by an impact on Mars that reaccreted in Martian orbit,[239] similar to the
[prevailing theory](/wiki/Giant_impact_hypothesis "Giant impact hypothesis")
for the origin of Earth's moon. Although the [VNIR](/wiki/VNIR "VNIR") spectra
of the moons of Mars resemble those of outer-belt asteroids, the [thermal
infrared](/wiki/Thermal_infrared "Thermal infrared") spectra of Phobos are
reported to be inconsistent with [chondrites](/wiki/Chondrite "Chondrite") of
any class.[238]

Mars may have moons smaller than 50 to 100 metres (160 to 330 ft) in diameter,
and a dust ring is predicted to exist between Phobos and Deimos.[22]

## Exploration

Main article: [Exploration of Mars](/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars "Exploration of
Mars")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/HiRISE_image_of_MSL_during_EDL_%28refined%29.png/220px-
HiRISE_image_of_MSL_during_EDL_%28refined%29.png)](/wiki/File:HiRISE_image_of_MSL_during_EDL_\(refined\).png)

[](/wiki/File:HiRISE_image_of_MSL_during_EDL_\(refined\).png "Enlarge")

The descent stage of the [Mars Science
Laboratory](/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory "Mars Science Laboratory") mission
carrying the [_Curiosity_ rover](/wiki/Curiosity_\(rover\) "Curiosity
\(rover\)") deploys its parachutes to decelerate itself before landing,
photographed by _[Mars Reconnaissance
Orbiter](/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter")_.

Dozens of crewless [spacecraft](/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft"), including
[orbiters](/wiki/Orbiter "Orbiter"), [landers](/wiki/Mars_lander "Mars
lander"), and [rovers](/wiki/Mars_rover "Mars rover"), have been sent to Mars
by the [Soviet Union](/wiki/Soviet_space_program "Soviet space program"), the
[United States](/wiki/NASA "NASA"), [Europe](/wiki/ESA "ESA"), and
[India](/wiki/ISRO "ISRO") to study the planet's surface, climate, and
geology.

As of
2021[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mars&action=edit),
Mars is host to eleven functioning [spacecraft](/wiki/Spacecraft
"Spacecraft"): eight in orbit - _[2001 Mars Odyssey](/wiki/2001_Mars_Odyssey
"2001 Mars Odyssey")_ , _[Mars Express](/wiki/Mars_Express "Mars Express")_ ,
_[Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter](/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Mars
Reconnaissance Orbiter")_ , _[MAVEN](/wiki/MAVEN "MAVEN")_ , _[Mars Orbiter
Mission](/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission "Mars Orbiter Mission")_ , _[ExoMars Trace
Gas Orbiter](/wiki/ExoMars_Trace_Gas_Orbiter "ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter")_ ,
[Emirates Mars Mission](/wiki/Emirates_Mars_Mission "Emirates Mars Mission")
and _[Tianwen-1](/wiki/Tianwen-1 "Tianwen-1")_ - and three on the surface -
the [Mars Science Laboratory](/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory "Mars Science
Laboratory") _[Curiosity](/wiki/Curiosity_\(rover\) "Curiosity \(rover\)")_
rover, the _[InSight](/wiki/InSight "InSight")_ lander and the
[_Perseverance_](/wiki/Perseverance_\(rover\) "Perseverance \(rover\)") rover.
The public can request images of Mars via the _Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter_ 's
[HiWish program](/wiki/HiWish_program "HiWish program").

The [Mars Science Laboratory](/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory "Mars Science
Laboratory"), named _Curiosity_ , launched on 26 November 2011, and reached
Mars on 6 August 2012 [UTC](/wiki/UTC "UTC"). It is larger and more advanced
than the [Mars Exploration Rovers](/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover "Mars
Exploration Rover"), with a movement rate up to 90 metres (300 ft) per
hour.[240] Experiments include a laser chemical sampler that can deduce the
make-up of rocks at a distance of 7 metres (23 ft).[241] On 10 February 2013,
the [_Curiosity_ rover](/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory "Mars Science
Laboratory") obtained the first deep rock samples ever taken from another
planetary body, using its on-board drill.[242] The same year, it discovered
that Mars's soil contains between 1.5% and 3% water by mass (albeit attached
to other compounds and thus not freely accessible).[243] Observations by the
_[Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter](/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Mars
Reconnaissance Orbiter")_ had previously revealed the possibility of flowing
water during the warmest months on Mars.[244]

On 24 September 2014, [Mars Orbiter Mission](/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission "Mars
Orbiter Mission") (MOM), launched by the [Indian Space Research
Organisation](/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation "Indian Space Research
Organisation") (ISRO), reached Mars orbit. ISRO launched MOM on 5 November
2013, with the aim of analyzing the Martian atmosphere and topography. The
Mars Orbiter Mission used a [Hohmann transfer
orbit](/wiki/Hohmann_transfer_orbit "Hohmann transfer orbit") to escape
Earth's gravitational influence and catapult into a nine-month-long voyage to
Mars. The mission is the first successful Asian interplanetary mission.[245]

The [European Space Agency](/wiki/European_Space_Agency "European Space
Agency"), in collaboration with [Roscosmos](/wiki/Roscosmos "Roscosmos"),
launched the [ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter](/wiki/ExoMars_Trace_Gas_Orbiter
"ExoMars Trace Gas Orbiter") and [_Schiaparelli_
lander](/wiki/Schiaparelli_EDM_lander "Schiaparelli EDM lander") on 14 March
2016.[246] While the Trace Gas Orbiter successfully entered Mars orbit on 19
October 2016, _Schiaparelli_ crashed during its landing attempt.[247]

In May 2018, NASA's _InSight_ lander was launched, along with the twin
[MarCO](/wiki/Mars_Cube_One "Mars Cube One") [CubeSats](/wiki/CubeSat
"CubeSat") that flew by Mars and acted as [telemetry](/wiki/Telemetry
"Telemetry") relays during the landing. The mission arrived at Mars in
November 2018.[248][249] InSight detected potential seismic activity (a
"[marsquake](/wiki/Marsquake "Marsquake")") in April 2019.[250][251]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/PIA23140-Mars-
InsightLander-Panorama-12092018.jpg/1000px-PIA23140-Mars-InsightLander-
Panorama-12092018.jpg)](/wiki/File:PIA23140-Mars-InsightLander-
Panorama-12092018.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:PIA23140-Mars-InsightLander-Panorama-12092018.jpg "Enlarge")

InSight Lander – panorama (9 December 2018)

In 2019, [MAVEN](/wiki/MAVEN "MAVEN") spacecraft mapped high-altitude global
wind patterns at Mars for the first time.[252][253] It was discovered that the
winds which are miles above the surface retained information about the land
forms below.[252]

### Future

Main article: [Exploration of Mars § Timeline of Mars
exploration](/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars#Timeline_of_Mars_exploration
"Exploration of Mars")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Orion_docked_to_Mars_Transfer_Vehicle.jpg/220px-
Orion_docked_to_Mars_Transfer_Vehicle.jpg)](/wiki/File:Orion_docked_to_Mars_Transfer_Vehicle.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:Orion_docked_to_Mars_Transfer_Vehicle.jpg "Enlarge")

Concept for a Bimodal Nuclear Thermal Transfer Vehicle in low Earth orbit

[NASA](/wiki/NASA "NASA") launched the [Mars 2020](/wiki/Mars_2020 "Mars
2020") mission on 30 July 2020.[254] The rover
_[Perseverance](/wiki/Perseverance_\(rover\) "Perseverance \(rover\)")_ and
_[Ingenuity](/wiki/Ingenuity_\(helicopter\) "Ingenuity \(helicopter\)")_
successfully landed on the surface of Mars on 18 February 2021. The mission
will cache samples for future retrieval and return of them to Earth. The
current concept for the [Mars sample-return mission](/wiki/Mars_sample-
return_mission "Mars sample-return mission") would launch in 2026 and feature
hardware built by NASA and ESA.[255] The [European Space
Agency](/wiki/European_Space_Agency "European Space Agency") will launch the
[ExoMars rover](/wiki/ExoMars_rover "ExoMars rover") and [surface
platform](/wiki/ExoMars_2020_surface_platform "ExoMars 2020 surface platform")
sometime between August and October 2022.[256]

The United Arab Emirates' _[Mars Hope](/wiki/Emirates_Mars_Mission "Emirates
Mars Mission")_ orbiter was launched on 19 July 2020, and successfully entered
orbit around Mars on 9 February 2021.[257] The probe will conduct a global
study of the Martian atmosphere.[258] With this accomplishment, UAE became the
second country, after India, to reach Mars on its first attempt.

Several plans for a [human mission to Mars](/wiki/Human_mission_to_Mars "Human
mission to Mars") have been proposed throughout the 20th and 21st centuries,
but no human mission has yet launched. [SpaceX](/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX") founder
[Elon Musk](/wiki/Elon_Musk "Elon Musk") [presented a
plan](/wiki/SpaceX_Mars_transportation_infrastructure "SpaceX Mars
transportation infrastructure") in September 2016 to, optimistically, launch a
crewed mission to Mars in 2024 at an estimated development cost of US$10
billion, but this mission is not expected to take place before 2027.[259] In
October 2016, President [Barack Obama](/wiki/Barack_Obama "Barack Obama")
renewed United States policy to pursue the goal of sending humans to Mars in
the 2030s, and to continue using the [International Space
Station](/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") as a
technology incubator in that pursuit.[260][261] The NASA Authorization Act of
2017 directed NASA to get humans near or on the surface of Mars by the early
2030s.[262]

## Astronomy on Mars

Main article: [Astronomy on Mars](/wiki/Astronomy_on_Mars "Astronomy on Mars")

See also: [Solar eclipses on Mars](/wiki/Solar_eclipses_on_Mars "Solar
eclipses on Mars")

With the presence of various orbiters, landers, and rovers, it is possible to
practice [astronomy](/wiki/Astronomy "Astronomy") from Mars. Although Mars's
moon [Phobos](/wiki/Phobos_\(moon\) "Phobos \(moon\)") appears about one-third
the [angular diameter](/wiki/Angular_diameter "Angular diameter") of the [full
moon](/wiki/Full_moon "Full moon") on Earth, [Deimos](/wiki/Deimos_\(moon\)
"Deimos \(moon\)") appears more or less star-like, looking only slightly
brighter than Venus does from Earth.[263]

Various phenomena seen from Earth have also been observed from Mars, such as
[meteors](/wiki/Meteor "Meteor") and [auroras](/wiki/Aurora "Aurora").[264]
The [apparent sizes](/wiki/Angular_diameter "Angular diameter") of the moons
Phobos and Deimos are sufficiently smaller than that of the Sun; thus, their
partial "eclipses" of the Sun are best considered
[transits](/wiki/Transit_\(astronomy\) "Transit \(astronomy\)") (see [transit
of Deimos](/wiki/Transit_of_Deimos_from_Mars "Transit of Deimos from Mars")
and [Phobos](/wiki/Transit_of_Phobos_from_Mars "Transit of Phobos from Mars")
from Mars).[265][266] [Transits of Mercury](/wiki/Transit_of_Mercury_from_Mars
"Transit of Mercury from Mars") and [Venus](/wiki/Transit_of_Venus "Transit of
Venus") have been observed from Mars. A [transit of
Earth](/wiki/Transit_of_Earth_from_Mars "Transit of Earth from Mars") will be
seen from Mars on 10 November 2084.[267]

On 19 October 2014, [comet Siding Spring](/wiki/C/2013_A1_\(Siding_Spring\)
"C/2013 A1 \(Siding Spring\)") passed extremely close to Mars, so close that
the [coma](/wiki/Coma_\(cometary\) "Coma \(cometary\)") may have enveloped
Mars.[268][269][270][271][272][273]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/PIA21260_-_Earth_and_Its_Moon%2C_as_Seen_From_Mars.jpg/309px-
PIA21260_-_Earth_and_Its_Moon%2C_as_Seen_From_Mars.jpg)](/wiki/File:PIA21260_-_Earth_and_Its_Moon,_as_Seen_From_Mars.jpg)

Earth and the Moon ( _[MRO](/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Mars
Reconnaissance Orbiter")_ [HiRISE](/wiki/HiRISE "HiRISE"), November 2016)[274]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/15-ml-06-phobos2-A067R1.jpg/168px-15-ml-06-phobos2-A067R1.jpg)](/wiki/File:15-ml-06-phobos2-A067R1.jpg)

[Phobos](/wiki/Phobos_\(moon\) "Phobos \(moon\)")
[transits](/wiki/Transit_of_Phobos_from_Mars "Transit of Phobos from Mars")
the Sun ( _[Opportunity](/wiki/Opportunity_\(rover\) "Opportunity \(rover\)")_
, 10 March 2004)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/PIA19801-TrackingSunspotsOnTheSunFromMars-20150708.gif/302px-
PIA19801-TrackingSunspotsOnTheSunFromMars-20150708.gif)](/wiki/File:PIA19801-TrackingSunspotsOnTheSunFromMars-20150708.gif)

Tracking [sunspots](/wiki/Sunspot "Sunspot") from Mars

## Viewing

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif/220px-
Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif)](/wiki/File:Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif)

[](/wiki/File:Apparent_retrograde_motion_of_Mars_in_2003.gif "Enlarge")

Animation of the apparent retrograde motion of Mars in 2003 as seen from
Earth.

The mean [apparent magnitude](/wiki/Apparent_magnitude "Apparent magnitude")
of Mars is +0.71 with a standard deviation of 1.05.[12] Because the orbit of
Mars is eccentric, the magnitude at [opposition](/wiki/Opposition_\(planets\)
"Opposition \(planets\)") from the Sun can range from about −3.0 to −1.4.[275]
The minimum brightness is magnitude +1.86 when the planet is in
[conjunction](/wiki/Conjunction_\(astronomy\) "Conjunction \(astronomy\)")
with the Sun.[12] At its brightest, Mars (along with [Jupiter](/wiki/Jupiter
"Jupiter")) is second only to Venus in luminosity.[12] Mars usually appears
distinctly yellow, orange, or red. [NASA](/wiki/NASA "NASA")'s _Spirit_ rover
has taken pictures of a greenish-brown, mud-colored landscape with blue-grey
rocks and patches of light red sand.[276] When farthest away from Earth, it is
more than seven times farther away than when it is closest. When least
favorably positioned, it can be lost in the Sun's glare for months at a time.
At its most favorable times — at 15-year or 17-year intervals, and always
between late July and late September — a lot of surface detail can be seen
with a [telescope](/wiki/Telescope "Telescope"). Especially noticeable, even
at low magnification, are the [polar ice caps](/wiki/Polar_ice_cap "Polar ice
cap").[277]

As Mars approaches opposition, it begins a period of [retrograde
motion](/wiki/Apparent_retrograde_motion "Apparent retrograde motion"), which
means it will appear to move backwards in a looping motion with respect to the
background stars. The duration of this retrograde motion lasts for about 72
days, and Mars reaches its peak luminosity in the middle of this motion.[278]

### Closest approaches

#### Relative

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Animation_of_Mars_orbit_around_Earth.gif/220px-
Animation_of_Mars_orbit_around_Earth.gif)](/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_orbit_around_Earth.gif)

[](/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_orbit_around_Earth.gif "Enlarge")

Geocentric animation of Mars's orbit relative to Earth from January 2003 to
January 2019  
Mars ***** Earth

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Mars_distance_from_Earth.svg/220px-
Mars_distance_from_Earth.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Mars_distance_from_Earth.svg)

[](/wiki/File:Mars_distance_from_Earth.svg "Enlarge")

Mars distance from Earth in millions of km (Gm).

The point at which Mars's geocentric longitude is 180° different from the
Sun's is known as [opposition](/wiki/Opposition_\(planets\) "Opposition
\(planets\)"), which is near the time of closest approach to Earth. The time
of opposition can occur as much as 8.5 days away from the closest approach.
The distance at close approach varies between about 54 and 103 million km (34
and 64 million mi) due to the planets' [elliptical](/wiki/Ellipse "Ellipse")
orbits, which causes comparable variation in [angular size](/wiki/Angular_size
"Angular size").[279][280] The second-to-last Mars opposition occurred on 27
July 2018,[281] at a distance of about 58 million km (36 million mi).[282] The
last Mars opposition occurred on 13 October 2020, at a distance of about 63
million km (39 million mi).[282] The average time between the successive
oppositions of Mars, its [synodic period](/wiki/Synodic_period "Synodic
period"), is 780 days; but the number of days between the dates of successive
oppositions can range from 764 to 812.[283]

As Mars approaches opposition it begins a period of [retrograde
motion](/wiki/Apparent_retrograde_motion "Apparent retrograde motion"), which
makes it appear to move backwards in a looping motion relative to the
background stars. The duration of this retrograde motion is about 72 days.

#### Absolute, around the present time

Mars made its closest approach to Earth and maximum apparent brightness in
nearly 60,000 years, 55,758,006 km (0.37271925 AU; 34,646,419 mi),
[magnitude](/wiki/Magnitude_\(astronomy\) "Magnitude \(astronomy\)") −2.88, on
27 August 2003, at 09:51:13 UTC. This occurred when Mars was one day from
opposition and about three days from its [perihelion](/wiki/Perihelion
"Perihelion"), making it particularly easy to see from Earth. The last time it
came so close is estimated to have been on 12 September [57,617
BC](/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic "Middle Paleolithic"), the next time being in
2287.[284] This record approach was only slightly closer than other recent
close approaches. For instance, the minimum distance on 22 August 1924, was
0.37285 [AU](/wiki/Astronomical_unit "Astronomical unit"), and the minimum
distance on 24 August 2208, will be 0.37279 [AU](/wiki/Astronomical_unit
"Astronomical unit").[203]

Every 15 to 17 years, Mars comes into opposition near its perihelion. These
perihelic oppositions make a closer approach to earth than other oppositions
which occur every 2.1 years. Mars comes into perihelic opposition in 2003,
2018 and 2035, with 2020 and 2033 being close to perihelic opposition.

## Historical observations

Main article: [History of Mars observation](/wiki/History_of_Mars_observation
"History of Mars observation")

The history of observations of Mars is marked by the oppositions of Mars when
the planet is closest to Earth and hence is most easily visible, which occur
every couple of years. Even more notable are the perihelic oppositions of
Mars, which occur every 15 or 17 years and are distinguished because Mars is
close to perihelion, making it even closer to Earth.

### Ancient and medieval observations

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Galileo.arp.300pix.jpg/220px-
Galileo.arp.300pix.jpg)](/wiki/File:Galileo.arp.300pix.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:Galileo.arp.300pix.jpg "Enlarge")

[Galileo Galilei](/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei"), first person to
see Mars via telescope in 1610.[285]

The ancient [Sumerians](/wiki/Sumer "Sumer") believed that Mars was
[Nergal](/wiki/Nergal "Nergal"), the god of war and plague.[286] During
Sumerian times, Nergal was a minor deity of little significance,[286] but,
during later times, his main cult center was the city of
[Nineveh](/wiki/Nineveh "Nineveh").[286] In Mesopotamian texts, Mars is
referred to as the "star of judgement of the fate of the dead."[287] The
existence of Mars as a wandering object in the night sky was recorded by the
ancient [Egyptian astronomers](/wiki/Egyptian_astronomy "Egyptian astronomy")
and, by 1534 BCE, they were familiar with the [retrograde
motion](/wiki/Apparent_retrograde_motion "Apparent retrograde motion") of the
planet.[288] By the period of the [Neo-Babylonian Empire](/wiki/Neo-
Babylonian_Empire "Neo-Babylonian Empire"), the [Babylonian
astronomers](/wiki/Babylonian_astronomy "Babylonian astronomy") were making
regular records of the positions of the planets and systematic observations of
their behavior. For Mars, they knew that the planet made 37 [synodic
periods](/wiki/Orbital_period "Orbital period"), or 42 circuits of the zodiac,
every 79 years. They invented arithmetic methods for making minor corrections
to the predicted positions of the planets.[289][290] In [Ancient
Greece](/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece"), the planet was known as
Πυρόεις.[291]

In the fourth century BCE, [Aristotle](/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") noted that
Mars disappeared behind the Moon during an [occultation](/wiki/Occultation
"Occultation"), indicating that the planet was farther away.[292]
[Ptolemy](/wiki/Ptolemy "Ptolemy"), a Greek living in
[Alexandria](/wiki/Alexandria "Alexandria"),[293] attempted to address the
problem of the orbital motion of Mars. Ptolemy's model and his collective work
on astronomy was presented in the multi-volume collection
_[Almagest](/wiki/Almagest "Almagest")_ , which became the authoritative
treatise on [Western
astronomy](/wiki/History_of_astronomy#Medieval_Western_Europe "History of
astronomy") for the next fourteen centuries.[294] Literature from ancient
China confirms that Mars was known by [Chinese
astronomers](/wiki/Chinese_astronomy "Chinese astronomy") by no later than the
fourth century BCE.[295] In the [East Asian](/wiki/East_Asian "East Asian")
cultures, Mars is traditionally referred to as the "fire star" (Chinese: 火星),
based on the [Five elements](/wiki/Five_elements_\(Chinese_philosophy\) "Five
elements \(Chinese philosophy\)").[296][297][298]

During the seventeenth century, [Tycho Brahe](/wiki/Tycho_Brahe "Tycho Brahe")
measured the [diurnal parallax](/wiki/Diurnal_parallax "Diurnal parallax") of
Mars that [Johannes Kepler](/wiki/Johannes_Kepler "Johannes Kepler") used to
make a preliminary calculation of the relative distance to the planet.[299]
When the telescope became available, the diurnal parallax of Mars was again
measured in an effort to determine the Sun-Earth distance. This was first
performed by [Giovanni Domenico Cassini](/wiki/Giovanni_Domenico_Cassini
"Giovanni Domenico Cassini") in 1672. The early parallax measurements were
hampered by the quality of the instruments.[300] The only
[occultation](/wiki/Occultation "Occultation") of Mars by Venus observed was
that of 13 October 1590, seen by [Michael Maestlin](/wiki/Michael_Maestlin
"Michael Maestlin") at [Heidelberg](/wiki/Heidelberg "Heidelberg").[301] In
1610, Mars was viewed by Italian astronomer [Galileo
Galilei](/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei"), who was first to see it via
telescope.[285] The first person to draw a map of Mars that displayed any
terrain features was the Dutch astronomer [Christiaan
Huygens](/wiki/Christiaan_Huygens "Christiaan Huygens").[302]

### Martian "canals"

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Karte_Mars_Schiaparelli_MKL1888.png/200px-
Karte_Mars_Schiaparelli_MKL1888.png)](/wiki/File:Karte_Mars_Schiaparelli_MKL1888.png)

Map of Mars by Giovanni Schiaparelli

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Lowell_Mars_channels.jpg/200px-
Lowell_Mars_channels.jpg)](/wiki/File:Lowell_Mars_channels.jpg)

Mars sketched as observed by Lowell before 1914 (south on top)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Mars_HST_Mollweide_map_1999.png/200px-
Mars_HST_Mollweide_map_1999.png)](/wiki/File:Mars_HST_Mollweide_map_1999.png)

Map of Mars from the _[Hubble Space Telescope](/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope
"Hubble Space Telescope")_ as seen near the 1999 opposition (north on top)

Main article: [Martian canal](/wiki/Martian_canal "Martian canal")

By the 19th century, the resolution of telescopes reached a level sufficient
for surface features to be identified. A perihelic opposition of Mars occurred
on 5 September 1877. In that year, the Italian astronomer [Giovanni
Schiaparelli](/wiki/Giovanni_Schiaparelli "Giovanni Schiaparelli") used a 22
centimetres (8.7 in) telescope in [Milan](/wiki/Milan "Milan") to help produce
the first detailed map of Mars. These maps notably contained features he
called _canali_ , which were later shown to be an [optical
illusion](/wiki/Optical_illusion "Optical illusion"). These _canali_ were
supposedly long, straight lines on the surface of Mars, to which he gave names
of famous rivers on Earth. His term, which means "channels" or "grooves", was
popularly mistranslated in English as "canals".[303][304]

Influenced by the observations, the orientalist [Percival
Lowell](/wiki/Percival_Lowell "Percival Lowell") founded an
[observatory](/wiki/Lowell_Observatory "Lowell Observatory") which had 30 and
45 centimetres (12 and 18 in) telescopes. The observatory was used for the
exploration of Mars during the last good opportunity in 1894 and the following
less favorable oppositions. He published several books on Mars and life on the
planet, which had a great influence on the public.[305][306] The _canali_ were
independently found by other astronomers, like [Henri Joseph
Perrotin](/wiki/Henri_Joseph_Perrotin "Henri Joseph Perrotin") and [Louis
Thollon](/wiki/Louis_Thollon "Louis Thollon") in Nice, using one of the
largest telescopes of that time.[307][308]

The seasonal changes (consisting of the diminishing of the polar caps and the
dark areas formed during Martian summer) in combination with the canals led to
speculation about life on Mars, and it was a long-held belief that Mars
contained vast seas and vegetation. The telescope never reached the resolution
required to give proof to any speculations. As bigger telescopes were used,
fewer long, straight _canali_ were observed. During an observation in 1909 by
[Camille Flammarion](/wiki/Camille_Flammarion "Camille Flammarion") with an 84
centimetres (33 in) telescope, irregular patterns were observed, but no
_canali_ were seen.[309]

Even in the 1960s, articles were published on Martian biology, putting aside
explanations other than life for the seasonal changes on Mars. Detailed
scenarios for the metabolism and chemical cycles for a functional ecosystem
have been published.[310]

### Spacecraft visitation

Main article: [Exploration of Mars](/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars "Exploration of
Mars")

Once [spacecraft](/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft") visited the planet during
NASA's [Mariner missions](/wiki/Mariner_program "Mariner program") in the
1960s and 1970s, these concepts were radically broken. The results of the
Viking life-detection experiments aided an intermission in which the
hypothesis of a hostile, dead planet was generally accepted.[311]

Mariner 9 and Viking allowed better maps of Mars to be made using the data
from these missions, and another major leap forward was the [Mars Global
Surveyor](/wiki/Mars_Global_Surveyor "Mars Global Surveyor") mission, launched
in 1996 and operated until late 2006, that allowed complete, extremely
detailed maps of the Martian topography, magnetic field and surface minerals
to be obtained.[312] These maps are available online; for example, at [Google
Mars](/wiki/Google_Mars "Google Mars"). [Mars Reconnaissance
Orbiter](/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter "Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter") and
[Mars Express](/wiki/Mars_Express "Mars Express") continued exploring with new
instruments and supporting lander missions. NASA provides two online tools:
[Mars Trek](/w/index.php?title=Mars_Trek&action=edit&redlink=1 "Mars Trek
\(page does not exist\)"), which provides visualizations of the planet using
data from 50 years of exploration, and [Experience
Curiosity](/wiki/Experience_Curiosity "Experience Curiosity"), which simulates
traveling on Mars in 3-D with Curiosity.[313]

## In culture

Main articles: [Mars in culture](/wiki/Mars_in_culture "Mars in culture") and
[Mars in fiction](/wiki/Mars_in_fiction "Mars in fiction")

[![Mars
symbol.svg](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Mars_symbol.svg/70px-
Mars_symbol.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Mars_symbol.svg)

Mars is named after the [Roman](/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome") [god of
war](/wiki/Mars_\(mythology\) "Mars \(mythology\)"). In different cultures,
Mars represents masculinity and youth. [Its symbol](/wiki/Gender_symbol
"Gender symbol"), a circle with an arrow pointing out to the upper right, is
used as a symbol for the male gender.

The many failures in Mars exploration probes resulted in a satirical counter-
culture blaming the failures on an Earth-Mars "[Bermuda
Triangle](/wiki/Bermuda_Triangle "Bermuda Triangle")", a "[Mars
Curse](/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars#Mars_Curse "Exploration of Mars")", or a
"Great Galactic Ghoul" that feeds on Martian spacecraft.[314]

### Intelligent "Martians"

The fashionable idea that Mars was populated by intelligent
[Martians](/wiki/Martian "Martian") exploded in the late 19th century.
[Schiaparelli's](/wiki/Giovanni_Schiaparelli "Giovanni Schiaparelli") "canali"
observations combined with [Percival Lowell](/wiki/Percival_Lowell "Percival
Lowell")'s books on the subject put forward the standard notion of a planet
that was a drying, cooling, dying world with ancient civilizations
constructing irrigation works.[315]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Kirks_Soap_Yerkes_Mars.jpg/170px-
Kirks_Soap_Yerkes_Mars.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kirks_Soap_Yerkes_Mars.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:Kirks_Soap_Yerkes_Mars.jpg "Enlarge")

An 1893 soap ad playing on the popular idea that Mars was populated

Many other observations and proclamations by notable personalities added to
what has been termed "Mars Fever".[316] In 1899, while investigating
atmospheric radio noise using his receivers in his Colorado Springs lab,
inventor [Nikola Tesla](/wiki/Nikola_Tesla "Nikola Tesla") observed repetitive
signals that he later surmised might have been radio communications coming
from another planet, possibly Mars. In a 1901 interview, Tesla said:

> It was some time afterward when the thought flashed upon my mind that the
> disturbances I had observed might be due to an intelligent control. Although
> I could not decipher their meaning, it was impossible for me to think of
> them as having been entirely accidental. The feeling is constantly growing
> on me that I had been the first to hear the greeting of one planet to
> another.[317]

Tesla's theories gained support from [Lord Kelvin](/wiki/Lord_Kelvin "Lord
Kelvin") who, while visiting the United States in 1902, was reported to have
said that he thought Tesla had picked up Martian signals being sent to the
United States.[318] Kelvin "emphatically" denied this report shortly before
leaving: "What I really said was that the inhabitants of Mars, if there are
any, were doubtless able to see New York, particularly the glare of the
electricity."[319]

In a _[New York Times](/wiki/New_York_Times "New York Times")_ article in
1901, [Edward Charles Pickering](/wiki/Edward_Charles_Pickering "Edward
Charles Pickering"), director of the [Harvard College
Observatory](/wiki/Harvard_College_Observatory "Harvard College Observatory"),
said that they had received a telegram from [Lowell
Observatory](/wiki/Lowell_Observatory "Lowell Observatory") in
[Arizona](/wiki/Arizona "Arizona") that seemed to confirm that Mars was trying
to communicate with Earth.[320]

> Early in December 1900, we received from Lowell Observatory in Arizona a
> telegram that a shaft of light had been seen to project from Mars (the
> Lowell observatory makes a specialty of Mars) lasting seventy minutes. I
> wired these facts to Europe and sent out neostyle copies through this
> country. The observer there is a careful, reliable man and there is no
> reason to doubt that the light existed. It was given as from a well-known
> geographical point on Mars. That was all. Now the story has gone the world
> over. In Europe, it is stated that I have been in communication with Mars,
> and all sorts of exaggerations have spring up. Whatever the light was, we
> have no means of knowing. Whether it had intelligence or not, no one can
> say. It is absolutely inexplicable.[320]

Pickering later proposed creating a set of mirrors in [Texas](/wiki/Texas
"Texas"), intended to signal Martians.[321]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/War-of-the-worlds-
tripod.jpg/240px-War-of-the-worlds-tripod.jpg)](/wiki/File:War-of-the-worlds-
tripod.jpg)

[](/wiki/File:War-of-the-worlds-tripod.jpg "Enlarge")

Martian tripod illustration from the 1906 French edition of _[The War of the
Worlds](/wiki/The_War_of_the_Worlds "The War of the Worlds")_ by [H. G.
Wells](/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells")

In recent decades, the high-resolution mapping of the surface of Mars,
culminating in [Mars Global Surveyor](/wiki/Mars_Global_Surveyor "Mars Global
Surveyor"), revealed no artifacts of habitation by "intelligent" life, but
pseudoscientific speculation about intelligent life on Mars continues from
commentators such as [Richard C. Hoagland](/wiki/Richard_C._Hoagland "Richard
C. Hoagland"). Reminiscent of the _canali_ controversy, these speculations are
based on small scale features perceived in the spacecraft images, such as
"pyramids" and the "[Face on Mars](/wiki/Cydonia_\(Mars\) "Cydonia
\(Mars\)")". Planetary astronomer [Carl Sagan](/wiki/Carl_Sagan "Carl Sagan")
wrote:

> Mars has become a kind of mythic arena onto which we have projected our
> Earthly hopes and fears.[304]

The depiction of Mars in fiction has been stimulated by its dramatic red color
and by nineteenth-century scientific speculations that its surface conditions
might support not just life but intelligent life.[322] Thus originated a large
number of [science fiction](/wiki/Science_fiction "Science fiction")
scenarios, among which is [H. G. Wells](/wiki/H._G._Wells "H. G. Wells")'
_[The War of the Worlds](/wiki/The_War_of_the_Worlds "The War of the Worlds")_
, published in 1898, in which Martians seek to escape their dying planet by
invading Earth.

Influential works included [Ray Bradbury](/wiki/Ray_Bradbury "Ray Bradbury")'s
_[The Martian Chronicles](/wiki/The_Martian_Chronicles "The Martian
Chronicles")_ , in which human explorers accidentally destroy a Martian
civilization, [Edgar Rice Burroughs](/wiki/Edgar_Rice_Burroughs "Edgar Rice
Burroughs")' [_Barsoom_ series](/wiki/Barsoom "Barsoom"), [C. S.
Lewis](/wiki/C._S._Lewis "C. S. Lewis")' novel _[Out of the Silent
Planet](/wiki/Out_of_the_Silent_Planet "Out of the Silent Planet")_
(1938),[323] and a number of [Robert A. Heinlein](/wiki/Robert_A._Heinlein
"Robert A. Heinlein") stories before the mid-sixties.[324]

[Jonathan Swift](/wiki/Jonathan_Swift "Jonathan Swift") made reference to the
moons of Mars, about 150 years before their actual discovery by [Asaph
Hall](/wiki/Asaph_Hall "Asaph Hall"), detailing reasonably accurate
descriptions of their orbits, in the 19th chapter of his novel _[Gulliver's
Travels](/wiki/Gulliver%27s_Travels "Gulliver's Travels")_.[325]

A comic figure of an intelligent Martian, [Marvin the
Martian](/wiki/Marvin_the_Martian "Marvin the Martian"), appeared in
_[Haredevil Hare](/wiki/Haredevil_Hare "Haredevil Hare")_ (1948) as a
character in the [Looney Tunes](/wiki/Looney_Tunes "Looney Tunes") [animated
cartoons](/wiki/Animated_cartoon "Animated cartoon") of [Warner
Brothers](/wiki/Warner_Brothers "Warner Brothers"), and has continued as part
of popular culture to the present.[326]

After the [Mariner](/wiki/Mariner_program "Mariner program") and
[Viking](/wiki/Viking_program "Viking program") spacecraft had returned
pictures of Mars as it really is, an apparently lifeless and canal-less world,
these ideas about Mars had to be abandoned, and a vogue for accurate, realist
depictions of human colonies on Mars developed, the best known of which may be
[Kim Stanley Robinson](/wiki/Kim_Stanley_Robinson "Kim Stanley Robinson")'s
[_Mars_ trilogy](/wiki/Mars_trilogy "Mars trilogy"). Pseudo-scientific
speculations about the [Face on Mars](/wiki/Cydonia_\(Mars\) "Cydonia
\(Mars\)") and other enigmatic landmarks spotted by [space
probes](/wiki/Space_probe "Space probe") have meant that ancient civilizations
continue to be a popular theme in science fiction, especially in film.[327]

## Interactive Mars map

![Map of
Mars](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Mars_Map.JPG/620px-
Mars_Map.JPG)

[](/wiki/File:Mars_Map.JPG "Enlarge")

![The image above contains clickable
links](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Interactive_icon.svg/12px-
Interactive_icon.svg.png)[Interactive image map](/wiki/Image_map "Image map")
of the [global topography of Mars](/wiki/Geography_of_Mars "Geography of
Mars"). Hover your mouse over the image to see the names of over 60 prominent
geographic features, and click to link to them. Coloring of the base map
indicates relative [elevations](/wiki/Elevation "Elevation"), based on data
from the [Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter](/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Laser_Altimeter
"Mars Orbiter Laser Altimeter") on NASA's _[Mars Global
Surveyor](/wiki/Mars_Global_Surveyor "Mars Global Surveyor")_. Whites and
browns indicate the highest elevations (+12 to +8 km); followed by pinks and
reds (+8 to +3 km); yellow is 0 km; greens and blues are lower elevations
(down to −8 km). [Axes](/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system "Cartesian
coordinate system") are [latitude](/wiki/Latitude "Latitude") and
[longitude](/wiki/Longitude "Longitude"); [Polar
regions](/wiki/Geographical_pole "Geographical pole") are noted.

(See also: _[Mars Rovers
map](/wiki/Template:Features_and_artificial_objects_on_Mars "Template:Features
and artificial objects on Mars")_ and _[Mars Memorial
map](/wiki/Template:Features_and_memorials_on_Mars "Template:Features and
memorials on Mars")_ ) ([view](/wiki/Template:Mars_map "Template:Mars map") •
[discuss](/wiki/Template_talk:Mars_map "Template talk:Mars map"))

## Notes

  1. **^** This image was taken by the [_Rosetta_](/wiki/Rosetta_\(spacecraft\) "Rosetta \(spacecraft\)") spacecraft's [Optical, Spectroscopic, and Infrared Remote Imaging System](/wiki/Optical,_Spectroscopic,_and_Infrared_Remote_Imaging_System "Optical, Spectroscopic, and Infrared Remote Imaging System") (OSIRIS), at a distance of ≈240,000 kilometres (150,000 mi) during its February 2007 encounter. The view is centered on the [Aeolis quadrangle](/wiki/Aeolis_quadrangle "Aeolis quadrangle"), with [Gale crater](/wiki/Gale_\(crater\) "Gale \(crater\)"), the landing site of the [_Curiosity_ rover](/wiki/Curiosity_\(rover\) "Curiosity \(rover\)"), prominently visible just left of center. The darker, more heavily cratered terrain in the south, [Terra Cimmeria](/wiki/Terra_Cimmeria "Terra Cimmeria"), is composed of older terrain than the much smoother and brighter [Elysium Planitia](/wiki/Elysium_Planitia "Elysium Planitia") to the north. Geologically recent processes, such as the possible existence of a [global ocean](/wiki/Water_on_Mars "Water on Mars") in Mars's past, could have helped lower-elevated areas, such as Elysium Planitia, retain a more youthful look.
  2. ^ _**a**_ _**b**_ _**c**_ Best-fit [ellipsoid](/wiki/Ellipsoid "Ellipsoid")
